# Cardano (ADA) | Kiln docs

circle-exclamation

**Please ensure to stake at least 4 ADA to be above the minimum value.**

When you decide to delegate your ADA to a stake pool for the first time, there are costs to consider:

1.  **Stake Address Registration Deposit:**
    
    *   You need to register your stake address on the blockchain, which requires a refundable deposit of **2 ADA**. This deposit is returned to you if you ever choose to deregister your stake address.
        
    
2.  **Transaction Fees:**
    
    *   There is a transaction fee for processing the delegation, usually around **0.17 to 0.3 ADA**.
        
    

This means that when you start staking with **4 ADA**, only about **1.7 ADA** will be effectively staked.

On the `/stake/ada` page of the dashboard you can check staking information about the network and stake your ADA in a few clicks with an intuitive onboarding.

Select the Account you want to stake on, the validator to delegate to, the amount of ADA you wish to stake and connect your wallet to stake!

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FPpsmYX38NuoENDw9tPdb%252FScreenshot%25202023-09-21%2520at%252019.00.16.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D54466da2-d6f8-4eaa-a5ff-fb9c3807b664&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d441966e&sv=2)

ADA stake page

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/staking/cardano-ada#stake-with-fireblocks-raw-signing-api)

Stake with Fireblocks raw signing API

circle-info

Transactions using the Fireblocks Raw Signing API are only enabled on Kiln Dashboard per request for organizations that have passed a security review from the Kiln and Fireblocks team regarding your API user setup. [More informations](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/custody-platforms/stake-from-fireblocks#stake-from-kiln-dashboard-using-fireblocks-raw-signing-api)
. **To enable this for your organisation, please get in touch with the Kiln team.**

Once you have [setup your Fireblocks Vaultarrow-up-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/connect/sdk/getting-started#sdk-configuration)
, you can use your credentials to stake ADA using your Fireblocks Vault.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FVJVquxBOBpr9YMwWGSRn%252FScreenshot%25202026-01-19%2520at%252011.03.27.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9d7b5e6c-4949-406b-bc88-89210bce414b&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=26a129fc&sv=2)

Fireblocks connect

Some notes about Fireblocks raw signing:

1.  Due to technical limitations in Fireblocks API, the connection goes through Kiln's Fireblocks proxy
    
2.  No Fireblocks account information or associated secrets are stored within any of Kiln's services, including our dashboard
    
3.  We have ensured that no logs capture this sensitive data
    
4.  The operational design guarantees that these secrets are transmitted directly to the Fireblocks API, without any interim storage
    
5.  Please note that upon reloading the dashboard or selecting the 'disconnect wallet' option, the system terminates access to any Fireblocks-related information
    

After connecting and selecting your Fireblocks vault, simply choose the pool and click "stake." Before signing your transaction, decode it in [Minitelarrow-up-right](https://ada.minitel.app/)
 or your preferred decoding tool. Carefully review and confirm that the decoded transaction details match your intended action.

In Minitel, you can paste your transaction's raw message content, retrievable from your Fireblocks console, to decode it.

For a complete walkthrough, check out the demo below.

[PreviousStakingchevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/staking)
[NextCelestia (TIA)chevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/staking/celestia-tia)

# Risks | Kiln docs

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/risks#smart-contract-risk)

**Smart contract risk**

It is important to acknowledge the inherent risk that the Kiln smart contracts may contain vulnerabilities or bugs.

Our smart contracts have undergone comprehensive audits conducted by industry leaders such as Spearbit and Quantstamp. Access reports and read more about our security practices [herearrow-up-right](https://security.kiln.fi/)
 and [here](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/audits-and-bug-bounty)
.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/risks#blockchain-protocol-risk)

**Blockchain protocol risk**

Ethereum and other supported EVM chains, are rapidly evolving technologies developed by decentralized collectives, operating independently of any central authority such as Kiln. It is important to note that, due to their nascent stage, they may contain potential errors or vulnerabilities. Consequently, these vulnerabilities could pose fund loss issue to the whole users of their networks.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/risks#defi-protocol-risk)

DeFi protocol risk

Each supported DeFi protocol of the Kiln DeFi product are developed and maintained independently to Kiln. They may contain potential errors or vulnerabilities which could impact user funds. It is important to highlight the risk of each protocol to the end users so they can take proper informed decisions.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/risks#rewards-variation-risk)

Rewards variation risk

DeFi protocols rewards rate, especially for lending supplying and liquidity provisioning, is highly dependent of the protocol liquidity and usage (for example the fewer the borrowing demand the less the supply rewards rate), and may present a lot of variance over time. This is independent from Kiln or the protocol itself and is purely do to market conditions and usage. Users of Kiln DeFi might see their rewards increase in high volatility market phases and diminish when the volatility get lowers without any possible guarantee.

[PreviousSecuritychevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security)
[NextAudits & Bug Bountychevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/audits-and-bug-bounty)

Last updated 1 year ago

Was this helpful?

*   [Smart contract risk](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/risks#smart-contract-risk)
    
*   [Blockchain protocol risk](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/risks#blockchain-protocol-risk)
    
*   [DeFi protocol risk](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/risks#defi-protocol-risk)

# OmniVaults | Kiln docs

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults#kiln-omnivaults)

Kiln OmniVaults


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln OmniVaults is a suite of smart contracts that our partners can use to enable native integration of DeFi protocols into their wallets or platforms. The solution is 100% onchain, fully automated, and provides a simplified integration. Utilize the Kiln API for native integration directly within your platform or customize our [widget](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/widget)
 to fit your needs.

The platform is currently integrated with many [protocols](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/supported-protocols)
 allowing partners to leverage Kiln's tech stack to offer these services to their end users

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FAo5akdx3r378Jo68Wvin%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db36300b5-17ed-4bef-b23d-4568bac61f39&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9f2a32f6&sv=2)

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults#values)

Values


------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln OmniVaults is designed with the same principles as other smart contract-based products:

*   **Transparency**: All actions, including deposits, withdrawals, and fee dispatching, occur on-chain and are easily trackable via event emissions.
    
*   **Security**: The audited contracts are secured with numerous on-chain and off-chain safety measures in place to protect users' funds and rewards.
    
*   **Flexibility**: Integrators can choose from multiple DeFi protocol integration types and create custom offerings.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults#project-licence)

Project Licence


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln OmniVaults is under the [BUSL-1.1 licencearrow-up-right](https://spdx.org/licenses/BUSL-1.1.html)
, some smart contract public interfaces are under [MIT licencearrow-up-right](https://spdx.org/licenses/MIT.html)
.

[PreviousSmart Contract interactionschevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/deprecated-dedicated-validators/smart-contract-interactions)
[NextHow to integrate?chevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate)

# Sei (SEI) | Kiln docs

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/sei-sei#validators)

Validators


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Mainnet

Name

Address

Kiln

[seivaloper1uxlf7mvr8nep3gm7udf2u9remms2jyjq6ee35garrow-up-right](https://www.mintscan.io/sei/validators/seivaloper1uxlf7mvr8nep3gm7udf2u9remms2jyjq6ee35g)

Kiln (legacy)

[seivaloper1u9xeaqdjz3kky2ymdhdsn0ra5uy9tc3eqkjc8warrow-up-right](https://www.mintscan.io/sei/validators/seivaloper1u9xeaqdjz3kky2ymdhdsn0ra5uy9tc3eqkjc8w)

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/sei-sei#overview)

Overview


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Metric

Value

**Stake activation time**

Instant

**Unbonding time**

21 days

**Re-delegating activation time**

Redelegation is instant, but creates a cooldown. After moving stake from a source validator to a destination validator, you can’t redelegate from this source or target validator until the chain’s unbonding period ends.

**Auto-compounding**

No

**Rewards frequency**

Rewards are distributed block-by-block

**Active set**

Top 40 by voting power

**Slashing**

Yes, up to 5% of stake can be slashed in the case of double signing. Up to 0.01% in the case of extended downtime.

**Block time**

300ms

**Minimum stake amount**

0.000001 SEI

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/sei-sei#staking-workflow)

Staking workflow


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**How does staking work?**

On Cosmos chains such as Sei, token holders choose a validator to delegate a select amount of tokens to. The delegator initiates a delegation transaction, which involves locking their tokens in a smart contract. These tokens are then counted towards the validator's total stake.

**What is the staking process?**

After the delegation has been initiated, SEIs are changed to validator shares of the validator you delegate to.

**Do funds move out to another wallet?**

Staked SEIs are not part of the balance anymore, but they don’t go to another address.

**Can I keep staking/unstaking from/to the same wallet?**

Yes, you can increase the staked amount or unstake part of it at anytime.

**Can I select how much of my wallet balance I want to stake?**

Yes, you select the amount of tokens you want to stake to earn rewards.

**How do I unstake?**

You can unstake by unbonding your funds. After you initiated the process:

• You stop receiving staking rewards

• It will take 21 days for the amount to be liquid

• But you will be able to cancel the unbonding process anytime, as this chain currently supports the function

**Can I unstake part of the staked balance?**

Yes, you can select the amount of tokens you want to unstake (this takes 21 days).

**How is my balance computed at epoch N for the rewards distribution?**

The balance computed at block N for the rewards distribution is the balance at block N.

**What is the slashing risk on Sei?**

Downtime: During a block window (108,000 blocks) if a validator signed less than 5% of the blocks, he will get jailed for 10 min but will not be slashed. No rewards can be earned during that jail time. Double signing: When a validator attests to two different blocks, it will face slashing. Stakers who have delegated to the slashed validator will not incur a reduction in their stake but the validator won't ever be able to earn rewards again. Delegators will have to redelegate to another validator in order for their stake to earn rewards again..

**How is commission paid?**

Commissions are paid to the validator at the same frequency than the reward distribution (every block).

[PreviousPolygon (POL - ex MATIC)chevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/polygon-pol-ex-matic)
[NextSolana (SOL)chevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/solana-sol)

Last updated 1 month ago

# Solana Watcher | Kiln docs

Streamline your Solana staking operations with "Solana Stake Watch"

Previously, when staking SOL with Kiln validators outside the Kiln Dashboard, customers had to manually import stakes to access reporting and ensure rebates.

This manual process is no longer necessary, thanks to our latest feature: "Solana Stake Watch."

In the wallet section, you can now view added wallets and add new ones, even before your first staking operation. Once added, you will find the list of watched wallets on the account page on the Solana tab.

All Solana stakes from these wallets will be automatically imported into the associated Kiln Dashboard Account, ensuring seamless reporting and rebates.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252F4KqhNsfFyrSYXeACZUJu%252Fimage%2520%2823%29.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D06db03da-b2ea-4169-818d-90c46028fbce&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=98fd6d6&sv=2)

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fkilnfi.slack.com%2Ffiles%2FU07KKT64A1J%2FF08HKNRQD5K%2Fsol_monitor_stake.mov&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9b793169&sv=2)

# Dashboard FAQs | Kiln docs

chevron-rightHow is the GRR shown for each protocol in the Dashboard calculated?[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/dashboard-faqs#how-is-the-grr-shown-for-each-protocol-in-the-dashboard-calculated)

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FdwfqON3p8LkfJY91IynR%252Fspaces_nye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng_uploads_vmTo9Vnus6hfze9mlPDD_Screenshot%25202024-12-04%2520at%252014.webp%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D62f1b0c0-9764-440c-92c7-5688d4bad355&width=300&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=2ad17c80&sv=2) For each protocol, the GRR is sourced from Kiln Connect through the `network_gross_apy` response in the protocol's `/network-stats` endpoint. See the [Kiln Connect FAQarrow-up-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/connect/kiln-connect-faqs#how-is-the-network_gross_apy-calculated-in-each-protocol-s-network-stats-endpoint)
 for details on `network_gross_apy` source and methodology.

`Historical GRR` is the average `GRR` of the account’s stakes

# Troubleshooting | Kiln docs

Here is a list of common issues and potential solutions for users of the [dashboardarrow-up-right](https://dashboard.kiln.fi/)
.

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/troubleshooting#i-cant-find-when-will-happen-the-next-skimming-event-on-one-of-my-eth-stakes)

I can't find when will happen the next skimming event on one of my ETH stakes


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In the Ethereum validator table in the reporting page, you can hover the reward amount on each line to see the estimated next skimming date and amount for each of your validators.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FlNsqxSU47oQ3LMnkTvXw%252FPhotopea%2520Online%2520Editor%2520Image.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbfb68598-07ef-4d8e-985d-3e7ce0a2aff3&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d7301c72&sv=2)

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/troubleshooting#dashboard-not-displaying-the-latest-total-amount-staked-and-total-rewards-earned-in-the-overview)

Dashboard not displaying the latest total amount staked and total rewards earned in the overview


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**The total amount staked and rewards values are cached and updated daily.** In the case you can't see the latest amount staked in the total amount. You can check when was the last update performed by placing your mouse over the "**Refresh"** button.

To force the refresh of these numbers to the current time, click the "**Refresh**" button. If the last updated time is not getting updated or if the issue persists contact your Kiln support team.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252Fvz2juMG6ccJrGk0sGVxV%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df9d23e6d-b52a-42a0-9bd3-b1ab9bd54e7d&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=e6223c92&sv=2)

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/troubleshooting#near-walletconnect-connection-issues)

NEAR WalletConnect connection issues


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**In order to connect a wallet, users need some tokens on the wallet they are trying to connect prior to connecting their wallet.** It is not possible to connect a NEAR wallet without NEAR on the wallet for example.

This is the error users get when connecting a wallet with 0 NEAR on it:

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252Fshlq5ovKrSyJEAUiEGZZ%252FScreenshot%25202024-04-17%2520at%252000.26.55.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Def7b89e6-d15d-4b02-b73c-2034eea4dd47&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c7184191&sv=2)

Upon connecting a NEAR wallet, you will be prompted to sign an **addKey** transaction. This transaction is required to interact with Kiln's pool contract. [Learn more.arrow-up-right](https://docs.near.org/concepts/protocol/access-keys#function-call-keys)

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/troubleshooting#signing-and-sending-transactions-with-fireblocks)

Signing and sending transactions with Fireblocks


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When signing and sending transactions, they may fail for different reasons:

*   **Users have not enough balance to pay for gas fees.**
    
*   **Users have misconfigured their Fireblocks TAP rules** so they cannot sign transactions (the transaction then shows as "Blocked by policy" within Fireblocks).
    
    *   Please follow [this TAP guidearrow-up-right](https://support.fireblocks.io/hc/en-us/articles/7354983580316-About-the-TAP)
         from Fireblocks.
        
    *   If you are using the Fireblocks Raw Signing API, get in touch with the Kiln support team for your TAP setup guide.
        
    *   Also note the Kiln batch deposit contract address on Ethereum [here](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/more-tools/eth-batch-deposit-contract)
        .
        
    
*   **There is an issue with the RPC used**, in this case please
    
    *   **Retry**, there are intermittent issues due to the underlying provider or blockchain.
        
    *   Contact your Kiln support team if the issue persists.
        
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/troubleshooting#eigenlayer-withdrawal-error-with-fireblocks)

EigenLayer Withdrawal Error with Fireblocks


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you're experiencing the following error when trying to withdraw from Eigenlayer using Fireblocks, even after whitelisting your EigenPod and DelayedWithdrawalRouter addresses, it might be related to the size of the transaction payload, particularly for the `verifyCheckpointProofs` transaction. The contract call data hex is too large for current Fireblocks setup, leading to the error.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252F8Atj0s89JpNJu5SHjAfO%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db8f8caa8-6898-48ff-bed5-67f59c0fb11d&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=37c19bab&sv=2)

Resolution steps:

*   Inform Fireblocks that you're experiencing issues with large transaction payloads from Eigenlayer.
    
*   Request that they "disable decoding of contract call data" for your workspace.
    

The resolution typically involves a manual setup adjustment on Fireblocks' end for your specific workspace. This allows their system to handle the large transaction payloads associated with Eigenlayer withdrawals.

[PreviousInvite a user to your organizationchevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/invite-a-user-to-your-organization)
[NextTutorialschevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/tutorials)

# Smart Contract interactions | Kiln docs

**We DO NOT recommend you proceed with this path unless you are an experienced user and have an urgent need to access the funds.**

**Note: If you are trying to interact with the contract via a Ledger device, Ledger Live does not work currently. We would recommend you connect it with a trusted browser wallet extension, for example Rabby Wallet. See** [**here**arrow-up-right](https://support.ledger.com/article/4409801559569-zd)
 **for more info.**

circle-exclamation

Following the [incident involving SwissBorgarrow-up-right](https://www.kiln.fi/post/sol-incident-swissborg---announcement)
, Kiln has implemented precautionary measures including [Orderly exiting of all Ethereum (ETH) validatorsarrow-up-right](https://www.kiln.fi/post/kiln-responds-to-infrastructure-issue-with-validator-exit-funds-remain-protected)
.

*   As a result, your staked ETH and rewards have been exited from staking and are now waiting to be withdrawn from the staking contract. However, the smart contract is not aware that these validators were exited, since the procedure was triggered outside the standard exit flow.
    
*   To ensure that your rewards can be properly withdrawn, you need to manually **finalize the exit of these validators by performing a** [**Request Exit**](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/deprecated-dedicated-validators/smart-contract-interactions#exit-validators-via-etherscan)
    . This can be done for all your validators in a single transaction.
    

We recommend performing theses actions inside Kiln UIs as documented here:

*   [Kiln dApparrow-up-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/wallets/stake-from-ledger-live/using-kiln-dapp/dedicated-validators/precautionary-validator-exit-and-withdraw-guide)
     guide with Ledger Live example
    
*   [Kiln Widgetarrow-up-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/wallets/stake-from-safe-wallet/how-to-stake-eth-on-safe-and-faq/precautionary-validator-exit-and-withdraw-guide)
     guide with Safe{Wallet} example
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/deprecated-dedicated-validators/smart-contract-interactions#exit-validators-via-etherscan)

Exit Validators via Etherscan

**Open Etherscan Dedicated Staking Contract page**

1.  Find your deposit transaction on your wallet transaction history.
    
    1.  Example: [https://etherscan.io/tx/0xb1f126e286275ae204106872c52a1d844eed1a837df61565f832055c46224634arrow-up-right](https://etherscan.io/tx/0xb1f126e286275ae204106872c52a1d844eed1a837df61565f832055c46224634)
        
    
2.  Scroll down to the _**Beaconchain Deposit**_ section where you can find all of your validators address.
    
    1.  Alternatively to Etherscan, you can also open your Tx hash in [Beaconcha.inarrow-up-right](https://beaconcha.in/tx/0xb1f126e286275ae204106872c52a1d844eed1a837df61565f832055c46224634)
        , where you can find more informations on your validators.
        
    2.  Keep a list of the pubKeys of your validators from all your deposits.
        
    
3.  From the Tx Hash on etherscran click the `To` address to open the smart contract page.
    
    1.  eg. [https://etherscan.io/address/0x1e68238ce926dec62b3fbc99ab06eb1d85ce0270arrow-up-right](https://etherscan.io/address/0x1e68238ce926dec62b3fbc99ab06eb1d85ce0270)
        
    
4.  Navigate to the `Contract` tab and the `Write as Proxy` , connect your wallet that did the initial deposit, paste one of your validators pubKeys in `13. requestValidatorsExit (0xb6b06dec)` and click **write**, this will exit the selected validators.
    
    1.  To exit multiple validators from Etherscan, you need to join pubKeys one after the other while **keeping 0x before the first one**, and r**emoving the 0x on all following pubKeys**.
        
        1.  eg. for 3 validators pubKeys:
            
            1.  `0x8e745317b728cbb16880ea4f78aa062501d87ff283b6420ca30cc0883e4b74f2cc27925c4b09dda182d4f73acdc45272`
                
            2.  `~0x~``9359b64f6afea36618a9f12a9099630352d7e4352e256b0f249cc5374ebb7bde0f77f71908bdeb29c5c1afc624661eb4`
                
            3.  `~0x~``8bc1b8b0b0f43cd75fef6921e5f14dbec2f14bfc8b64c8d9cdddf153623f005a5206b07ecaf5ac730484f587026c7fb6`
                
            
        2.  final string to input in etherscan `0x8e745317b728cbb16880ea4f78aa062501d87ff283b6420ca30cc0883e4b74f2cc27925c4b09dda182d4f73acdc45272``9359b64f6afea36618a9f12a9099630352d7e4352e256b0f249cc5374ebb7bde0f77f71908bdeb29c5c1afc624661eb4``8bc1b8b0b0f43cd75fef6921e5f14dbec2f14bfc8b64c8d9cdddf153623f005a5206b07ecaf5ac730484f587026c7fb6`
            
        
    2.  Once this transaction is signed and successful in your transaction history, you can track the validator exit status using the beaconproxy pages of a validator by just searching for your validator pubKey.
        
        1.  eg. [https://beaconcha.in/validator/0x8e745317b728cbb16880ea4f78aa062501d87ff283b6420ca30cc0883e4b74f2cc27925c4b09dda182d4f73acdc45272#depositsarrow-up-right](https://beaconcha.in/validator/0x8e745317b728cbb16880ea4f78aa062501d87ff283b6420ca30cc0883e4b74f2cc27925c4b09dda182d4f73acdc45272#deposits)
            
        
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/deprecated-dedicated-validators/smart-contract-interactions#withdraw-exited-validators-and-rewards-via-etherscan)

Withdraw exited validators & rewards via Etherscan

**Requirements : Your validators need to be exited, you need to have called** [**RequestExit**](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/deprecated-dedicated-validators/smart-contract-interactions#exit-validators-via-etherscan)
**.**

circle-info

To ensure that your rewards can be properly withdrawn, you need to manually **finalize the exit of these validators by performing a** [**Request Exit**](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/deprecated-dedicated-validators/smart-contract-interactions#exit-validators-via-etherscan)
. This can be done for all your validators in a single transaction.

1.  Open the smart contract page:
    
    1.  eg. [https://etherscan.io/address/0x1e68238ce926dec62b3fbc99ab06eb1d85ce0270arrow-up-right](https://etherscan.io/address/0x1e68238ce926dec62b3fbc99ab06eb1d85ce0270)
        
    
2.  Navigate to the `Contract` tab and the `Write as Proxy` , connect your wallet that did the initial deposit, paste one of your validator pubKey in `6. batchWithdrawCLFee (0x0ffab6c2)` and click **write**, this will withdraw rewards and principal exited from the selected validators.

# Stake from Squads | Kiln docs

You can stake your SOL holdings with our Solana validator directly from your Squads.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FPCMXsmCALiJrUQfuVS1q%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbb3fe2b4-30a1-4f8d-b8c0-ac5995938862&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=3a2f63ee&sv=2)

Validator Staking

**To stake SOL:**

1.  Launch your v4 or Legacy Squads from here: [https://squads.so/arrow-up-right](https://squads.so/)
    
2.  Navigate to the "Staking" tab and select the "Validator" section.
    
3.  Search for the Kiln validator and enter the amount of SOL you want to stake.
    
4.  Click on the "Stake" button and launch a transaction.
    
5.  Your SOL will be staked once the transaction has been executed. You will start earning rewards in the following epoch.
    
6.  The "Staked" tab in the "Validator" section allows you to check the staked SOL amount and track your staking returns.
    

**To unstake SOL:**

1.  Navigate to the "Staking" tab and select "Validator" section.
    
2.  Click on the "Staked" tab and then the Kiln validator.
    
3.  Click the "Unstake" button to launch a transaction.
    

Please note that due to nature of epochs, your unstaked SOL will be only be available for withdrawal after the end of the epoch.

1.  Your SOL stake account will be deactivated once the transaction has been executed. The deactivation period finishes with the start of the new epoch.
    
2.  Once the deactivation period finishes, you will be able to withdraw your SOL. Navigate to the "Staked" tab in the "Validator" section, click on the Kiln validator, and launch a transaction to complete the withdrawal.
    
3.  Your SOL will be returned to your vault once you have signed the transaction.
    

[PreviousUsing Kiln dAppchevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/wallets/stake-from-safe-wallet/using-kiln-dapp)
[NextCustody platformschevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/custody-platforms)

Last updated 1 year ago

# Pause | Kiln docs

Kiln actively monitors all deployed smart contracts for suspicious activity and promptly responds to incidents.

Partners can hold the PAUSER role for added control, while Kiln continues to monitor and collaborates with partner security teams for investigations.

Alternatively, partners may delegate the PAUSER role to Kiln, allowing Kiln to swiftly pause contracts in response to incidents, which some partners prefer for faster response times.

# Plan your integration | Kiln docs

Kiln is a powerful staking platform that can be used to enable staking and access to decentralized finance (DeFi) from your product. With Kiln, you or your clients can easily stake crypto assets, either manually or programmatically.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FY5HIdZTpe5OQq1MebCuN%252FIntegrators%2520%281%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd0f379af-b31b-4df4-bf33-7e7f860d9e52&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4a89a38c&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/plan-your-integration#seamlessly-integrate-staking-and-defi-with-kiln)

Seamlessly Integrate Staking and DeFi with Kiln

At Kiln, we understand the importance of a smooth integration process. Follow our project timeline to successfully incorporate Kiln's staking and DeFi capabilities into your platform.

circle-check

Kiln's team is here to help with :

*   Onboarding & Kick-Off meeting.
    
*   Recurring catch-up to plan together your integration.
    
*   A technical kick-off meeting with your engineering team.
    
    *   (They can already get started with our [Technical Documentationarrow-up-right](https://docs.api.kiln.fi/docs/quickstart)
         ⚙️).
        
    
*   Marketing, Legal, and Support material & best practice.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/plan-your-integration#project-timeline)

Project Timeline

**Phase 1: Setup (1-2 days)**

*   Activate your Kiln account on Kiln's Dashboard.
    
*   Familiarize yourself with Kiln's documentation, integration guides, and code samples.
    

**Phase 2: Planning and Design (1-2 weeks)**

*   Finalize decisions outlined in the planning considerations in consultation with impacted teams & working with Kiln's support team.
    
*   Identify the specific use cases and features you want to integrate (e.g., programmatic native staking, DeFi access, 32ETH staking, staking pools, or liquid staking token creation).
    
*   Define what the integration looks like; What is the deposit and withdraw flow and how does it fit with your existing products? You will find examples in this user documentation for each use-case.
    
*   Define success metrics for your integration (e.g., share of assets stake on my platform).
    
*   Determine the integration approach: Kiln Widget, Kiln API and SDK, or Kiln Smart Contracts.
    

**Phase 3: Build (2-4 weeks & optional)**

*   Build your frontend integration using Kiln's prebuilt UI components or create a customized earn flow in your platform.
    
*   Build your server-side integration to securely conduct staking and DeFi operations.
    
*   Integrate Kiln's reporting and reconciliation pipeline to centralize data on stakes, rewards, and operations.
    

**Phase 4: Training (1-2 days)**

*   Conduct team-specific training and create playbooks for the product you integrated, covering areas such as:
    
    *   Staking operations and DeFi management in your product.
        
    *   Customer support, User documentation and Marketing Kick-Off.
        
    

**Phase 5: Testing and Go-Live (1 week)**

*   Test your integration end-to-end in test and live environments using Kiln's testing tools and resources.
    
*   Make sure you measure user engagement and that your success metrics are covered by your team or by Kiln's Dashboard.
    
*   Go live with your integration, enabling your users to access staking and DeFi services seamlessly.
    
*   Roll out your user engagement campaigns to drive the first user deposits in your new product.
    

By following this project timeline and addressing the key considerations, you can ensure a smooth and successful integration of Kiln's staking and DeFi capabilities into your platform, providing your users with a seamless and secure experience.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/plan-your-integration#get-inspired-for-your-next-integration)

Get inspired for your next integration

[🔌Integrate Kiln productschevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/integrate-kiln-products)

[PreviousSafe CDchevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/more-tools/safe-cd)
[NextIntegrate Kiln productschevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/integrate-kiln-products)

# Glossary | Kiln docs

**Term**

**Definition**

Active Set

The current group of validators selected by the network to produce blocks and validate transactions.

Auto-compounding

Feature that automatically restakes earned staking rewards to maximize returns.

Baker

Validator in the Tezos network, responsible for producing blocks.

Baking

Process of producing blocks in Tezos, equivalent to validating in other PoS systems.

Delegation Node

A delegation node typically refers to a validator node that allows token holders (delegators) to assign their staking power to it without transferring ownership of their assets. By delegating to a node, users contribute to the network’s security and earn a portion of the staking rewards generated by the node’s validator activities. The delegation node operator manages the validator infrastructure, while delegators maintain control over their tokens.

DPoS (Delegated Proof-of-Stake)

Delegated Proof of Stake (DPoS) is a consensus mechanism used by some blockchains to secure the network and validate transactions. In a DPoS system, token holders vote to elect a small, trusted group of validators (often called _delegates_ or _block producers_) who are responsible for producing new blocks and maintaining the blockchain. Voting power is typically proportional to the number of tokens a participant holds.

Dual staking

A staking model requiring tokens from two different protocols. For example, Bitcoin and Core dual staking can yield higher rewards.

Epoch/Era

An epoch (or era, depending on the protocol) is a standardized period of time used by blockchain networks to organize key processes such as validator selection, reward distribution, and consensus updates.

Finality Provider

Node that ensures block finality and irreversibility in certain blockchain protocols.

Governance

On-chain or off-chain processes allowing token holders to vote on protocol upgrades and policies.

Max stake amount

Maximum amount of tokens that can be delegated to a validator or delegator.

Min stake amount

Minimum tokens required to participate in staking as a validator or delegator.

NPoS (Nominated Proof-of-Stake)

Nominated Proof-of-Stake (NPoS) is a consensus mechanism where token holders (nominators) select trusted validators to participate in block production and network security. Both nominators and validators share the rewards and potential risks, such as slashing, based on the validator’s performance.

Operator

An individual or organization that maintains validator infrastructure and manages technical operations.

PoS (Proof-of-Stake)

A consensus mechanism used by blockchain networks where participants, called **validators**, are responsible for proposing and validating new blocks. To participate, validators must lock up (or "stake") a certain amount of cryptocurrency as collateral.

PoS systems typically select validators through mechanisms that may consider factors such as the amount staked, randomness, or other protocol-specific criteria. Validators who act maliciously or fail to fulfill their duties can be penalized through slashing, which results in the loss of part or all of their staked tokens.

PPoS (Pure Proof-of-Stake)

Used by Algorand, this system randomly selects block proposers and validators based on their stake, using cryptography to ensure fairness and security. No one can cheat or collude to control the system, as selection happens privately and automatically.

Re-delegating activation time

Time it takes for a delegation to become active and start earning rewards.

Restaking

Restaking is the act of leveraging staked assets to provide security to multiple services simultaneously, increasing capital efficiency but introducing additional risks.

Rewards frequency

How often staking rewards are distributed (e.g., per block, daily, etc.).

Self-bond

Self-bond refers to the portion of tokens that a validator locks up from their own wallet to support their own validator node.

Signer

Validator in the Stacks (STX) network.

Slashing

Penalty mechanism for validators due to downtime or malicious behavior, causing loss of staked tokens.

Stake

The amount of cryptocurrency locked or delegated by a user to support network operations.

Stake activation time

Delay between staking tokens and when they become active and eligible to earn rewards.

Stake lock-up time

Period during which staked assets are locked and cannot be moved, often matching the unbonding period.

Staking Pool

Group of participants who combine tokens to stake collectively and share rewards.

Staking Rewards

Incentives earned for participating in network consensus, usually paid in the native token.

Unbonding time

Cooldown period after unstaking during which tokens remain locked before becoming transferable.

Unstake

The process of withdrawing tokens that were previously staked, often triggering a cooldown period.

Validators

A validator is a node operator responsible for participating in a blockchain network’s consensus mechanism. Validators propose and confirm new blocks, verify transactions, and help secure the network.

[PreviousLedger Live FAQchevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/working-with-kiln/support/faqs/ledger-live-faq)

Last updated 10 months ago

# Governance | Kiln docs

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/governance#vault-administration-partner)

Vault administration (partner)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Vaults are managed by partners using several key admin roles:

*   SYS\_ADMIN: wallet responsible for contract administration and other role attribution
    
*   FEE\_MANAGER: wallet responsible for changing the end user fee and the split between multiple recipients
    
*   FEE\_COLLECTOR: wallet responsible for claiming the commission
    
*   SANCTIONS\_MANAGER: wallet responsible for enabling the OFAC-sanctioned wallet check
    
*   CLAIM\_MANAGER: wallet responsible for claiming additional rewards from the lending protocols
    
*   PAUSER: wallet responsible for pausing all interaction with vault contracts, managed by Kiln as a security fail-safe
    
*   UNPAUSER: wallet responsible for unpausing the contract
    

It is recommended to have multi-sig wallets for these roles with a strong quorum security.

**NOTE**: You can only have 1 wallet assigned as SYS\_ADMIN, but multiple wallets assigned to all other roles.

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/governance#blocklist-administration-partner)

Blocklist administration (partner)


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln DeFi vaults feature custom [deposit blocklistsarrow-up-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/defi/security/compliance-features#blocklists)
 that partners can opt to use. The blocklist admin role is:

*   OPERATOR: wallet responsible for adding and removing addresses to and from the custom blocklist
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/governance#upgradability-structure-kiln)

Upgradability Structure (Kiln)


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FcbVj5bJKocTu0qKRp6dL%252FFrame%2520129%2520%282%29.svg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D45929e44-acb6-4269-a216-8324b0eaa412&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=ebbcf47d&sv=2)

Upgradability overview - dashed arrows are atomic actions - orange boxes are smart contract controlled by Kiln and green are controlled by partners

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/governance#kiln-defi-vaults)

Kiln DeFi Vaults

Kiln DeFi vaults follow the beacon proxy pattern where all vaults fetch their implementation address from a VaultUpgradeableBeacon smart contract.

This is administered by 4 roles:

*   PROXY\_ADMIN: a multisig quorum between Kiln and third parties responsible for attributing the below roles
    
*   PAUSER: a wallet responsible for pausing all interaction with vault contracts, managed by Kiln as a security failsafe
    
*   FREEZER: a multisig quorum between Kiln and third parties responsible for freezing Vault implementation (to make it non-upgradeable)
    
*   IMPLEMENTATION\_MANAGER: a multisig quorum between Kiln and third parties responsible for upgrading Vault implementations
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/governance#kiln-defi-connectors)

Kiln DeFi Connectors

Kiln DeFi Connectors also follow the beacon proxy pattern where each connector implementation address is fetched from a ConnectorRegistry contract.

This is administered by 4 roles:

*   ADMIN: a multisig quorum between Kiln and third parties responsible for attributing the below roles
    
*   PAUSER: a wallet responsible for pausing all interaction with connector contracts, managed by Kiln as a security failsafe
    
*   FREEZER: a multisig quorum between Kiln and third parties responsible for freezing connector implementations (to make some of them non-upgradeable)
    
*   CONNECTOR\_MANAGER: a multisig quorum between Kiln and third parties responsible for upgrading connectors implementation
    

[PreviousSmart contract interactionschevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/smart-contract-interactions)
[NextReporting datachevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/reporting-data)

# [Deprecated] Dedicated Validators | Kiln docs

circle-exclamation

This offering has been deprecated. Please refer to [Native ETH Stakingarrow-up-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~/revisions/4UAN6yWl2kl6UVohTDJW/kiln-products/onchain/native-eth-staking)
 for Pectra-compatible staking support.

Using Kiln Onchain Dedicated Staking smart contracts, partners can propose a dedicated staking offer to their users by connecting them to an Operator validator infrastructure with a fully onchain ETH staking solution.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252F0jD0rKVfZD8kQvbPy3yr%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da865c40a-52ff-4e19-9380-03c962240dd4&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a46e22d4&sv=2)

An Integration example on Ledger Enterprise

1.  **Easy to use** - users can stake any multiple of 32 ETH on dedicated validators in one transaction
    
2.  **Transparency first** - flow of funds, from deposit, to rewards, unstaking or commission dispatching is full visible and auditable onchain
    
3.  **Don't trust, verify** - anyone can verify that provisioned validators deposit data are valid, making the staking process more transparent and secure
    
4.  **Integrate in a few hours** - only a few contract interactions are required for the staking and unstaking flows, making it very convenient to integrate on your platform
    
5.  **Tokenize validators or not** - partners decide whether they want tokenize their validators to all users to transfer validator ownership.
    
6.  **Keep user fund segregation** \- Kiln Onchain Dedicated ensures that a user's staked balance remains completely separated from other user funds throughout the entire process, starting from the initial deposit to the final unstaking.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/deprecated-dedicated-validators#track-record)

Track record


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln Onchain dedicated solution has been in production with multiple partners since October 2022 and has seen **more than 480K ETH deposited**.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252F4jZF82oCdOScaE4JPCzQ%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D18a5698a-c203-44bc-90bc-d72a7ebcfc93&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4c8bc588&sv=2)

Ledger Live integration example over a year

You can explore publicly these product metrics with [dune dashboardarrow-up-right](https://dune.com/kiln/kiln-ledger-live)
.

# Business Continuity | Kiln docs

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/security/business-continuity#what-happens-if-kiln-goes-out-of-business)

**What happens if Kiln goes out of business?**


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In the unlikely event that Kiln becomes insolvent, we have a business continuity and disaster recovery plan which we were certified for as part of our successful SOC 2 Type II audits.

B2B customers of Kiln can retrieve pre-signed Ethereum validator exit messages which enables them to unilaterally unstake.

We also have an [Ethereum-specific policyarrow-up-right](https://drive.google.com/file/d/11BkzY_PLO9bKY2v7uND4D63oLqSrOiGE/view)
 involving exiting all validators or transferring validation keys in case Kiln can no longer operate the service.

[PreviousAudits & Bug Bountieschevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/security/audits-and-bug-bounties)
[NextSource codechevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/security/source-code)

# Onchain | Kiln docs

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FcYUbbvXaKvReLTmIsbus%252FKiln%2520Onchain%2520Latest.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2dab5190-1080-4506-b59b-6d0c041847c0&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=59e0829e&sv=2)

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain#the-problems-addressed-by-kiln-onchain)

The problems addressed by Kiln Onchain


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Offering non-custodial ETH staking** **is hard**, as Ethereum lacks an onchain commission system, platforms adopt two approaches: they either hold staked ETH or rewards to earn commissions, or they charge deposit fees rather than relying on staking rewards as an incentive.
    
2.  **Existing ETH offerings can be opaque** as the complete fund flow, including deposit handling, reward management, and commission distribution, isn't solely managed through transparent smart contract logic.
    
3.  **Introducing new use-cases on a validator infrastructure**, like solo staking, pooled staking, or validator NFTs, is challenging due to the absence of established standards for operators in these areas.
    
4.  **Create a custom staking offering for your platform**, customizing commissions from staking rewards, distributing them to partners, seamlessly integrating multiple operators, and even issuing Liquid Staking Tokens like NFTs or ERC20 tokens to represent users' staked positions.
    

Kiln Onchain is an audited suite of **smart contracts** that eliminates these barriers, enabling partners to offer fully branded, customisable, non-custodial Ethereum staking to end-users, whilst being able to monetise the offering. With Kiln Onchain, partners can now prioritise **user retention** and **earning a rewards share** from offering seamless Ethereum staking.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252F2VCD6NWqhVMwYHG83AJ2%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd79b7ba7-78b0-4715-8850-24bbb33ab7fa&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=b9bc2c79&sv=2)

Kiln Onchain suite

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain#introducing-kiln-onchain-platform)

Introducing Kiln Onchain platform


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln Onchain addresses three main actors:

1.  **Partners,** such as wallets and custodians, that want to create a custom staking solutions for their users. This may involve solo staking with one operator or proposing their own Liquid Staking Token with 2 operators.
    
2.  **Operators** are Ethereum validator providers who integrate their validator infrastructure via smart contracts, enabling them to offer staking services like pooling or dedicated staking, and accept deposits from multiple integration partners.
    
3.  **Stakers** are ETH holders seeking to engage in Ethereum protocol staking, and they can choose between pooled solutions or dedicated staking. Throughout the entire staking process, they retain custody of their assets, ensuring a fully transparent and auditable fund flow.
    

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FTQVsEeXfTGXTGFUyE5HQ%252FBackgrounds%2520Frame%25202.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2f32a01b-84a3-49ec-b04c-cd93f391911c&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=e0cd5fd2&sv=2)

Kiln Onchain offers a suite of smart contracts designed to allow partners to accommodate a wide range of use cases within native and pooled staking. Currently, there are **four distinct options** available:

1.  **Dedicated Validators**: Native ETH protocol staking in batches of 32 ETH, providing a dedicated and secure staking solution.
    
2.  **Tokenized Validators**_:_ ‘Dedicated Validators’, but with the ability to tokenize the validator to benefit from liquidity and flexibility without needing to fully unstake or exit the validator.
    
3.  **Staking Pool**: Enables partners to offer services that allow staking any amount of ETH, without the issuance of a transferrable receipt token.
    
4.  **Liquid Staking**: Same as Staking Pooling but with the ability to issue a custom transferrable receipt token that represents the withdrawal credentials and the ownership of the users stake.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain#values)

Values


---------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are multiple ways partners can propose staking to their users (Stakers) through the Onchain platform (pooled, dedicated, ...), but the underlying principles remain the same across all the components of this product:

1.  **Transparency**: deposits, commissions dispatching or exits, everything happens onchain and is easy to track via Event emissions and simple view functions everyone can call.
    
2.  **Security**: staking through this audited solution is designed to be non-custodial (_\* some parts will be upgradable for a certain timeframe_), and a lot of onchain and offchain safety guards are in place to protect users funds and rewards.
    
3.  **Flexibility**: partners have the choice between multiple staking integration types and can create their custom offering with or without liquidity tokens, or with one or multiple operators.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain#project-licence)

Project Licence


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln Onchain is under the [BUSL-1.1 licencearrow-up-right](https://spdx.org/licenses/BUSL-1.1.html)
, some smart contract public interfaces are under [MIT licencearrow-up-right](https://spdx.org/licenses/MIT.html)
.

[NextNative ETH Stakingchevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/onchain/native-eth-staking)

# Smart contract interactions | Kiln docs

circle-exclamation

Kiln OmniVaults smart contracts integrate the [Chainalysis Oracle for sanctions screeningarrow-up-right](https://go.chainalysis.com/chainalysis-oracle-docs.html)
 on all chains where it's available. The oracle actively monitors and screens addresses against up-to-date sanctions lists, ensuring that any sanctioned addresses are automatically restricted from interacting with Kiln OmniVaults vaults.

Kiln OmniVaults Vault smart contracts adhere to the [ERC4626arrow-up-right](https://docs.openzeppelin.com/contracts/4.x/erc4626)
 standard, making integration straightforward. When users deposit tokens, they receive shares representing their position. For a better user experience, we recommend abstracting any asset-to-share conversions and always displaying asset amounts on the UI instead of share amounts.

Here is the ABI of the Vault contract:

file-download

28KB

[vault.abi.json](https://1911902555-files.gitbook.io/~/files/v0/b/gitbook-x-prod.appspot.com/o/spaces%2Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%2Fuploads%2FXNZVviaAXZl0wa02nxYY%2Fvault.abi.json?alt=media&token=1819cb8b-00dd-4fbe-a9e9-0bfce3bfe8ee)

downloadDownload[arrow-up-right-from-squareOpen](https://1911902555-files.gitbook.io/~/files/v0/b/gitbook-x-prod.appspot.com/o/spaces%2Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%2Fuploads%2FXNZVviaAXZl0wa02nxYY%2Fvault.abi.json?alt=media&token=1819cb8b-00dd-4fbe-a9e9-0bfce3bfe8ee)

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/smart-contract-interactions#id-1.-depositing)

1\. Depositing


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Before depositing 'x' assets, ensure the user has approved the vault to spend 'x' on their behalf via the asset contract.

*   **Check Allowance**: Call the `allowance(address owner, address spender) → uint256` function on the ERC20 asset contract.
    
*   **Increase Allowance**: Use the `approve(address spender, uint256 amount) → bool` function on the ERC20 asset contract to increase the allowance to the desired deposit amount.
    

Before depositing X assets, you must make sure the user approved the vault to spend X on its behalf on the asset contract.

⚠️ **Note**: Only have the user approve the exact amount they intend to deposit into the vault.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FgYrC7QhKzzRgnVzezmFi%252FFrame%2520127%2520%283%29.svg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db4b58276-4e90-47d3-b993-392880790d32&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1b4a7d72&sv=2)

User deposits ERC20 and receives shares

To deposit an amount of the vault's ERC20, the transaction sender must call the `deposit(uint256 assets, address receiver)` function, where `assets` is the amount of ERC20 to deposit in the strategy, and `receiver` is the address that should own the deposited position.

(Optional) If you need to compute the amount of shares the user will receive before making a deposit, you can preview the amount by calling `previewDeposit(uint256 assets)`, where `assets` is the amount of ERC20 to deposit.

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/smart-contract-interactions#id-2.-get-the-balance-in-assets)

2\. Get the balance in assets


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

chevron-rightUsing the reporting API[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/smart-contract-interactions#using-the-reporting-api)

chevron-rightUsing contract view functions[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/smart-contract-interactions#using-contract-view-functions)

1.  To check the position balance in shares, call the `balanceOf(address owner)` function, where `owner` is the address of the position owner.
    
2.  To determine the amount of ERC20 the position is worth, call the `previewRedeem(uint256 shares)` function, where `shares` is the amount of shares to redeem. This will return the equivalent amount of ERC20.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/smart-contract-interactions#id-3.-exiting-a-position)

3\. Exiting a position


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/smart-contract-interactions#case-1-exit-part-of-a-position)

Case 1: exit part of a position

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252Fn9oNmOAwomgvJgOlw5Bw%252FFrame%2520128%2520%283%29.svg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db5f64c38-f63e-4e0f-9a8d-55cff9e08909&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=153d63ae&sv=2)

Withdraw ERC20 value using assets as input value

In this case, we expect the user to input the amount of ERC20 they want to withdraw and then call the `withdraw(uint256 assets, address receiver, address owner)` function. Here:

*   `assets` is the amount of ERC20 to withdraw.
    
*   `receiver` is the address that will receive the redeemed ERC20.
    
*   `owner` is the address of the position owner (the same as the transaction sender).
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/smart-contract-interactions#case-2-exit-a-position-fully)

Case 2: exit a position fully

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FeaFSdneKBhU3tyMXP5yL%252FFrame%2520128%2520%282%29.svg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0312dc12-0026-454c-b5ae-81b13d748648&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=722e8120&sv=2)

Redeem ERC20 value using shares as input value

To exit the entire position, the best approach is to determine the user's share amount and redeem it. Follow these steps:

1.  Retrieve the share amount of the user's position using the `balanceOf(address owner)` function, where `owner` is the address of the position owner.
    
2.  Redeem the shares by calling the `redeem(uint256 shares, address receiver, address owner)` function, where:
    
    *   `shares` is the amount of shares to redeem.
        
    *   `receiver` is the address that will receive the redeemed ERC20.
        
    *   `owner` is the address of the position owner (the same as the transaction sender).
        
    

circle-exclamation

Using the `withdraw` function instead of the `redeem` function may prevent the user from fully exiting their position, as the shares-to-assets rate might change between the input and the actual block when the transaction is included.

[PreviousHow to integrate?chevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate)
[NextGovernancechevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/how-to-integrate/governance)

# dApp | Kiln docs

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dapp#what-is-the-kiln-dapp)

What is the Kiln dApp?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The [Kiln dApparrow-up-right](https://stake.kiln.fi/)
     is a permissionless dApp allowing you to stake your ETH for dedicated validators and engage in EigenLayer Restaking.
    
*   It has a user-friendly interface where users can connect their wallets, choose how much to stake, and manage their staked assets.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dapp#what-are-the-main-advantages-of-the-kiln-dapp)

What are the main advantages of the Kiln dApp?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Key advantages of the Kiln dApp include:

*   1-Click staking - connect your wallet and stake in a single click.
    
*   Permissionless - simply connect your wallet to get started.
    
*   Lower Fees - at least 20% less than other leading providers.
    
*   Enterprise-Grade Service: SOC2, multi-cloud / region infrastructure, backed by uptime SLAs.
    
*   Non-Custodial: You retain exclusive access rights to your stake positions.

# Story (IP) | Kiln docs

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/story-ip#validators)

Validators


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Mainnet

Name

Address

Kiln

0x08629caABb138194272F952a1488879539472A11

Validator Addr.

[storyvaloper1pp3fe24mzwqegfe0j54pfzy8j5u5w2s3vpkfr8arrow-up-right](https://story.explorers.guru/validator/storyvaloper1pp3fe24mzwqegfe0j54pfzy8j5u5w2s3vpkfr8)

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/story-ip#overview)

Overview


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Metric

Description

Stake activation time

Instant

Auto-compounding

No

Minimum Stake

1024 IP

Unbonding time/Lockup period

14-day unlock period for all staking token types(locked or unlocked). During the unbonding period, the delegator/validator will not earn block rewards. But they may still be slashed.

Rewards frequency

The reward is accumulated per block and can be distributed per block. However, it will only be automatically distributed to the delegator’s account when it is larger than a threshold. The default and also minimal threshold is 8 IP, which means that only if the delegator’s reward is more than 8 IP, it will be sent to the delegator’s account

Active set

Yes, currently the top 64. Kilns validator will be in the active(bonded) set

Slashing

Yes

*   **Double signing**: Validators who sign a block twice are penalized with a 5% slash of staked tokens and permanent removal from the validator set. This prevents blockchain forks and compromises to consensus.
    
*   **Extended downtime**: Validators who are offline for a significant period (missing 95% of the last 28,800 blocks) face a 0.02% slash and temporary jailing.
    
*   **Insufficient self-delegation**: Validators with a stake below the 1,024 $IP minimum are jailed
    

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/story-ip#staking-workflow)

Staking workflow


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

How does staking work?

For every block, a fixed proportion of token inflation will go to the rewards distribution pool, which will be shared among all 64\* active validators according to each of their share weights. These allocated tokens will then be shared among the validator and its delegators in a fashion described by the next section. The validator share weight is calculated based on the total token staking amount, and whether or not the token staking type is locked or unlocked.

What is the staking process?

To start earning rewards, you will need to add your stake to the validator run by Kiln. If a fixed period is chosen, a delegation id will be returned to the users. Users must use this delegation id to unstake tokens from this stake operation. If flexible staking is chosen, the returned delegation id will be 0.

The staking amount needs to be larger than a threshold, which is 1024 IP.

Do funds move out to another wallet?

No

Can I keep staking/unstaking from/to the same wallet?

Yes, However, the redelegated tokens are still subject to the unbonding process(14 days)

Can I select how much of my wallet balance I want to stake?

Yes, you select the amount of tokens you want to stake to earn rewards.

Can I unstake a portion of my stake?

Partial unstake of a delegation is supported. For example, if a 1-year long delegation has 1 million tokens, after 1 year, users can unstake 500k from this delegation and keep the remaining staked to continue earning rewards.

Whats the difference between Locked v Unlocked Tokens?

Unlocked tokens have no restrictions imposed on them and can be used for gas consumption, transfers, and staking.

Unlike unlocked tokens, locked tokens cannot be transferred or traded and are unlocked based on an unlock schedule. However, locked tokens may be staked to earn staking rewards, with the locked staking reward rate being half of that of unlocked tokens.

Staked locked and unlocked tokens have the same voting power. That means that a validator with 100 staked locked tokens has the same network voting power as a validator with 100 staked unlocked tokens.

Delegators can decide how flexible and how long they want to stake their tokens. By default, for both locked and unlocked tokens, delegators can stake and then unstake immediately and get their token back after the unbonding time. This is called ‘Flexible Staking’.

Both types of tokens can be slashed if their validators get slashed.

How do I unstake?

When staking without a staking period, users can unstake anytime. The tokens will be distributed to the user’s account after the unbonding time.

A fee of 1 IP will be charged for unstaking to prevent spamming. The fee will be burnt by the contract.

The minimum unstaking amount is 1024 IP. After the unstaking request is processed, if the remaining staked amount is less than 1024 IP, the remaining part will also be unstaked together.

The unstaking request will first go through the unbonding process, which is 14 days. After that, the unbonded requests are sent to a withdrawal queue, distributing a maximum of 32 withdrawals per block. If there are more than 32 withdrawal requests in the withdrawal queue, the next 32 withdrawal requests will be processed in the next block.

What is the slashing risk on Story?

Validators must act honestly and perform well; otherwise, they risk being slashed (losing a portion of the stake entrusted by their delegators). Slashing occurs in two main scenarios:

1.  Downtime: This happens when a validator’s node is offline and misses 95% of the past 28,800 blocks. As a result, the validator is jailed. They can unjail and return to the active set, but their delegators will irrevocably lose 0.02% of their staked amount.
    

Double-signing: This occurs when a validator mishandles their key and signs one block twice. In this case, the validator is permanently jailed (tombstoned), and their delegators lose 5% of their tokens. It’s a significant and severe penalty, as the validator is removed from the network permanently.

[PreviousStacks (STX)chevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/stacks-stx)
[NextSui (SUI)chevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/sui-sui)

Last updated 1 month ago

Was this helpful?

*   [Validators](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/story-ip#validators)
    
*   [Overview](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/story-ip#overview)
    
*   [Staking workflow](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/validators/protocols/story-ip#staking-workflow)

# Celestia (TIA) | Kiln docs

circle-info

Auto-compounding of your staking rewards is available for TIA, please visit [these instructionsarrow-up-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/custodians/tutorials/cosmos-auto-compound-a-stake#how-to-make-an-auto-compounding-stake-through-kiln-dashboard)
 on how to enable it.

On the `/stake/tia` page of the dashboard you can check staking information about the network and stake your TIA in a few clicks with an intuitive onboarding.

Select the Account you want to stake on, the amount of TIA you wish to stake and connect your wallet to stake!

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252Fk3Y8qePP7JOi0Tu2ledD%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df98577d0-0739-4972-8beb-c1ce93f19470&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=3cdcdc56&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/staking/celestia-tia#staking-with-keplr-wallet)

Staking with Keplr Wallet

[Keplrarrow-up-right](https://www.keplr.app/)
 is a fast, secure, and user-friendly wallet designed for the Cosmos ecosystem. It seamlessly integrates with our platform, allowing you to stake TIA from Kiln Dashboard.

circle-check

[ForDeFIarrow-up-right](https://fordefi.com/)
 users can connect their wallet using this Keplr connectivity option.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FprInA53fgbtzC5ihFcRi%252FScreen%2520Recording%2520Aug%252026.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4ee2786a-2f76-45ac-90b5-41268f6c07cc&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=54b64d2d&sv=2)

This gif introduces the way to connect your Keplr Wallet on ATOM (Cosmos), TIA as a Cosmos chain follow the same process.

Step-by-step staking process from Kiln Dashboard:

1.  Connect your wallet:
    
    *   Click the "Connect Wallet" button on our platform.
        
    *   Select "Keplr" from the list of available options.
        
    *   Approve the connection request in the Keplr popup.
        
    
2.  Enter stake amount: Specify the amount of TIA you wish to stake.
    
3.  Confirm transaction: Review the details and confirm the staking transaction in the Keplr popup.
    
4.  Track your stake: Monitor your staked assets and rewards directly in Kiln Dashbord or through the Keplr dashboard.
    

circle-info

Please note that the signing flow is not yet compatible with hardware wallets like Ledger. If you are using a Ledger device, you can directly stake to Kiln from [Keplr dashboardarrow-up-right](https://wallet.keplr.app/chains/cosmos-hub?modal=staking&chain=cosmoshub-4&validator_address=cosmosvaloper1uxlf7mvr8nep3gm7udf2u9remms2jyjqvwdul2&step_id=2)
.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/staking/celestia-tia#staking-with-keplr-dashboard)

Staking with Keplr Dashboard

**Prerequisites :**

*   Connect your Ledger wallet to Keplr wallet/dashboard, [step by step videoarrow-up-right](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JyK8OWMtWk0)
     📼
    

**Staking with Keplr Dashboard :**

1.  From [Keplr dashboardarrow-up-right](https://wallet.keplr.app/chains/cosmos-hub)
    ; Select your asset and click stake
    
2.  Search Kiln validator and select it
    
3.  Click the stake button
    
4.  Follow the signing instruction in Keplr wallet and on your Ledger Device (make sure it's plugged-in)
    

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252FT44mHUnQAcp1KBBfFIXB%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd9f51fa5-9018-4da9-a42a-7c680e18d871&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=fd60fe6c&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/staking/celestia-tia#stake-with-fireblocks)

Stake with Fireblocks

circle-info

Transactions using the Fireblocks Raw Signing API are only enabled on Kiln Dashboard per request for organizations that have passed a security review from the Kiln and Fireblocks team regarding your API user setup. [More informations](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/integrations/custody-platforms/stake-from-fireblocks#stake-from-kiln-dashboard-using-fireblocks-raw-signing-api)
. **To enable this for your organisation, please get in touch with the Kiln team.**

Once you have [setup your Fireblocks Vaultarrow-up-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/connect/sdk/getting-started#sdk-configuration)
, you can use your credentials to stake TIA using your Fireblocks Vault.

![](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1911902555-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252Fnye3yqpuOzdfrtWAlwng%252Fuploads%252F06DeexRBk14eMIkUqAx5%252FScreenshot%25202026-01-19%2520at%252011.03.27.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D44c79e39-d781-486a-87aa-5766ffa42ca5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=6d7e6705&sv=2)

Some notes about Fireblocks raw signing:

1.  Due to technical limitations in Fireblocks API, the connection goes through Kiln's Fireblocks proxy
    
2.  No Fireblocks account information or associated secrets are stored within any of Kiln's services, including our dashboard
    
3.  We have ensured that no logs capture this sensitive data
    
4.  The operational design guarantees that these secrets are transmitted directly to the Fireblocks API, without any interim storage
    
5.  Please note that upon reloading the dashboard or selecting the 'disconnect wallet' option, the system terminates access to any Fireblocks-related information
    

* * *

After connecting and selecting your Fireblocks vault, simply choose the amount and click "stake." Before signing your transaction, decode it in [Minitelarrow-up-right](https://tia.minitel.app/)
 or your preferred decoding tool. Carefully review and confirm that the decoded transaction details match your intended action.

In Minitel, you can paste your transaction's raw message content, retrievable from your Fireblocks console, to decode it.

For a complete walkthrough, check out the demo below _\- The video below introduces the way to stake ATOM (Cosmos), TIA as a Cosmos chain follow the same process._

[PreviousCardano (ADA)chevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/staking/cardano-ada)
[NextCosmos (ATOM)chevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/dashboard/staking/cosmos-atom)

Last updated 1 month ago

# Compliance Features | Kiln docs

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/compliance-features#blocklists)

Blocklists


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln DeFi vaults have built-in compliance functionality to prevent specific addresses from interacting with them. As an integrator, it's possible for you to specify addresses you wish to prevent from interacting with your Kiln DeFi vaults, in addition to the default list of addresses externally maintained by Chainalysis. Addresses specified by you can be added to and removed from the blocklist at your request.

[hashtag](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/compliance-features#non-transferable-vault-shares)

Non-Transferable Vault Shares


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Kiln DeFi vault shares are non-transferable to other addresses, by default. Only the original depositor can redeem the associated share(s) for assets held in the vault. Upon request, vault shares can be made fully transferable or transferable only to specified addresses.

[PreviousSource codechevron-left](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/security/source-code)
[NextKiln OmniVaults Direct FAQchevron-right](https://docs.kiln.fi/v1/kiln-products/omnivaults/kiln-omnivaults-direct-faq)
